<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer9754700105234418352"><strong>Meet Bridget Jones</strong>—a 30-something Singleton who is certain she would have all the answers if she could:<br /><br /> a. lose 7 pounds<br /> b. stop smoking<br /> c. develop Inner Poise<br /><br /><br />"123 lbs. (how is it possible to put on 4 pounds in the middle of the night? Could flesh have somehow solidified becoming denser and heavier? Repulsive, horrifying notion), alcohol units 4 (excellent), cigarettes 21</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9754700105234418352"><strong>Meet Bridget Jones</strong>—a 30-something Singleton who is certain she would have all the answers if she could:<br /><br /> a. lose 7 pounds<br /> b. stop smoking<br /> c. develop Inner Poise<br /><br /><br />"123 lbs. (how is it possible to put on 4 pounds in the middle of the night? Could flesh have somehow solidified becoming denser and heavier? Repulsive, horrifying notion), alcohol units 4 (excellent), cigarettes 21 (poor but will give up totally tomorrow), number of correct lottery numbers 2 (better, but nevertheless useless)..."<br /><br /><em>Bridget Jones's Diary</em> is the devastatingly self-aware, laugh-out-loud daily chronicle of Bridget's permanent, doomed quest for self-improvement — a year in which she resolves to: reduce the circumference of each thigh by 1.5 inches, visit the gym three times a week not just to buy a sandwich, form a functional relationship with a responsible adult, and learn to program the VCR.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9754700105234418352">...more</a>

      $('edition_156658').observe('prototip:shown', function() {
        if (this.up('#box')) {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});

              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});

<div class="communityQuestion">
<div class="questionText">
<a href="/questions/515242-can-someone-please-explain-why-doesn-t-she">Can someone please explain why doesn't she use pronouns? Is this common anywhere, or in any situation?
 "...Wish was Dead. Am never, going to drink again for the rest of life... Could really fancy some chips..." (around 22% in)

*English is not my first language</a>
</div>
<div class="communityQAFooter questionFooter">
<ul class="questionFooterActions">
<li class="footerItem like">
<span id="like_container_community_question_515242" class="likeItContainer"><a href="/rating/voters/515242?resource_type=CommunityQuestion" rel="nofollow" id="like_count_community_question_515242"><span class="likesCount">3 likes</span></a> · <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F578596.Bridget_Jones_s_Diary" class="jsLike like_it" rel="nofollow">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class="footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp">
<a href="/questions/515242-can-someone-please-explain-why-doesn-t-she">4 months ago</a>
</li>
<li class="footerItem communityQuestionPermalink">
<a href="/questions/515242-can-someone-please-explain-why-doesn-t-she">See all 2 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

<div class="allCommunityAnswers">
<div class="communityAnswer">
<div class="communityAnswerBody">
<div class="answererUserIcon">
<a href="/user/show/22956742-kelly-louchart" class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto"><img src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/users/1387542449i/22956742._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" alt="" /></a>
</div>
<div class="communityAnswerTextContainer">
<span class="communityAnswererName">
<a href="/user/show/22956742-kelly-louchart">Kelly Louchart</a>
</span>
<span class="communityAnswerText">
It's a personal diary. No pronouns necessary. Some people use pronouns when they write in a diary; others don't. The author chose not to for Bridget.
</span>
</div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown">
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_8162009">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/8162009" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/419287-jessica" class="left imgcol" title="Jessica"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1289534648p2/419287.jpg" alt="Jessica" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/8162009?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 24, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/419287-jessica" class="user" title="Jessica">Jessica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/227443.Bridget_Jones_s_Diary" title="Paperback 9780140280098" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">chicks, and maybe non-chicks baffled by the chick mind</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/419287-jessica?shelf=crazy-ladies" class="actionLinkLite">crazy-ladies</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/419287-jessica?shelf=chicklits" class="actionLinkLite">chicklits</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer8162009">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13187631202478463812">I didn't enjoy this book in an ironic way, or in a it's-good-even-though-, or I-can't-believe-I-do-but-I-perversely-can't-help-it or any other angled, roundabout, halfway indirect from behind kind of way.... No. I sat on my couch and wolfed this thing down in one sitting while laughing my ass off.<br /><br />I read it last spring when I decided I was curious about what "chick-lit" was, so that I could form an opinion and generally improve my likelihood of passing as a somewhat informed member of civilizatio</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13187631202478463812">I didn't enjoy this book in an ironic way, or in a it's-good-even-though-, or I-can't-believe-I-do-but-I-perversely-can't-help-it or any other angled, roundabout, halfway indirect from behind kind of way.... No. I sat on my couch and wolfed this thing down in one sitting while laughing my ass off.<br /><br />I read it last spring when I decided I was curious about what "chick-lit" was, so that I could form an opinion and generally improve my likelihood of passing as a somewhat informed member of civilization. This was not the only "chick-lit" book I attempted. I tried *Bergdorf Blondes*, the first few pages of which made me want to stab my eyes out with a rusty fork; well, maybe it made me more want to stab someone else's eyes out (Plum Sykes springs to mind), but my point is that it wasn't just bad but actually highly disturbing. Disturbing as in, does not so much shake as demolish one's faith in humanity and makes one tremble in horror at the times we're evidently living in..... I also tried *Good in Bed*, which wasn't upsetting, but did seem pretty bad, or at least definitely not for me. I even flipped open a *Shopaholic* book, which wasn't as awfully written as *<a title="Bergdorf Blondes A Novel by Plum Sykes" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/381704.Bergdorf_Blondes_A_Novel">Bergdorf Blondes</a>* but did similarly make yearn for a grim Stalinist dystopia where this kind of trash just isn't permitted.<br /><br />Then there was Bridget Jones.<br /><br />Now, my enjoyment of this book was not uncomplicated by this terrifying "I-am-Cathy" feeling that I'm now enough of a grownup to identify with a lovably neurotic character from fluffy popular women's fiction. Because, dear bookster, identify I did. Yes. I had the 100% straightforward chick-lit experience, which I guess must be exactly this sense of recognizing your own ridiculously stereotypical feminine traits in a light novel's plucky heroine. And seriously? That's exactly what happened to me.<br /><br />(Can I just explain that I'm supposed to be packing right now, which is why this is getting so long and involved? I'm not really crazy, I'm just procrastinating.) (Also, though, I do want to tell you guys about Bridget Jones and how weirdly good it was.)<br /><br />There were a few things I didn't realize about BJ before I read this book. One is, she drinks too much. The other is, she smokes. I know it sounds dumb, but I think I would've felt differently knowing that, instead of just that she struggles with food. I'd sort of heard that a lot of it was about efforts to control her weight or whatever, and this typical, you know, on-again-off-again dieting, blah blah blah, and I really couldn't imagine anything less appealing, partly because that isn't a problem I identify with, and partly because does the world really need another book about a self-hating lady trying to lose weight? And why would anyone want to read something like that anyway?<br /><br />Well, I would. And I did! Because it's not really about her trying to lose weight (although I guess it kind of is), it's more about the constant, compulsive agony self-inflicted by a woman cursed not only with zero impulse control and a ravenous id, but also obsessively high standards for herself and a ridiculous amount of guilt and self-scrutiny about virtually everything she does.<br /><br />So yeah basically, this book is about me and a lot (not all) of my close female friends. And it really, really -- I want you to hear this from me -- truly gets at some stuff about certain ways that a lot of women tend to act and think, which, I'm sorry, all my fancy feminisms and gender theory aside, let's be honest, a lot (not all) of us are very crazy in some classically female ways, and Fielding just NAILS a lot of those. Plus she's very funny.<br /><br />Is this the greatest book ever written? No. But it was fun to read.<br /><br />Obviously, not all men act one way, and not all women act like Bridget Jones. However, I certainly do, and that must be the reason I got such a kick out of this book.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13187631202478463812">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer164160403">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13529202010346977602">Let's review this book the Bridget way!<br /><em> Reading goal for 2011: 35 books (not bad)<br />Books actually read: 38(v.g.) <br />No. of chick-lits supposed to be read in a year: 1 (fair)<br />No. of chick-lits actually read: 2 (including <strong> Bridget Jones's Diary </strong>) </em><br />But wait a second! Who can call <strong> <em> Bridget Jones's Diary </em> </strong> a chick-lit? That would be an insult to such a master-piece! No, Bridget is no wannabe chick-lit heroine and this book is certainly no trashy best-seller! <strong> <em> Bridget Jones's Diary </em> </strong> is definitely a piece</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13529202010346977602">Let's review this book the Bridget way!<br /><em> Reading goal for 2011: 35 books (not bad)<br />Books actually read: 38(v.g.) <br />No. of chick-lits supposed to be read in a year: 1 (fair)<br />No. of chick-lits actually read: 2 (including <strong> Bridget Jones's Diary </strong>) </em><br />But wait a second! Who can call <strong> <em> Bridget Jones's Diary </em> </strong> a chick-lit? That would be an insult to such a master-piece! No, Bridget is no wannabe chick-lit heroine and this book is certainly no trashy best-seller! <strong> <em> Bridget Jones's Diary </em> </strong> is definitely a piece of literature! It is well written, it's funny and it is extremely relate-able. Bridget, like most girls, tends to make mistakes, fall in love with the wrong guy and she gives an all new twist to the story of <strong> <em>'Pride and Prejudice' </em> </strong>. In a way, it is a work of plagiarism and yet, it has the quality of being original! It is at once the biggest tribute to Austen and one of the most successful experiments on creating a story which has its own elements of uniqueness and surprise!<br />And the best thing about this book is, you don't want to believe Bridget is not real! It's like Santa Claus or Hogwarts all over again! <br />Yes, I know I can't stop gushing over it but trust me, had this book been anything like the usual chick-lits, I most certainly wouldn't have given it a five-star rating! Of course, I approached it gingerly and rather hesitantly at first but once I was done, I felt like banging my head against the wall asking, "Why didn't I read it before when I had the e-book lying with me for the last three years?" <br />But I guess I had to borrow it from <strong> <em> Gayatri</em> </strong> and then spend an entire fortnight gushing over it! <br />Do I recommend it to you? Hell, yeah, I do!</span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Annalisa by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/540757-lori">Lori</a>
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=chick-lit" class="actionLinkLite">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=book-club" class="actionLinkLite">book-club</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer129300751">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9203531022062573106">I'm torn as to how to rate this. On the one hand, Fielding nails the humor. Humor is very hard to capture in literature and I often found myself smiling or chuckling. But when I wasn't, I was exasperated with Bridget Jones. Fielding nails her too. Why do women insist on being proud of being so... shallow? Idiotic, blind about themselves and their lives, and obsessed with all the wrong things in life? I didn't sympathize with Bridget at all, nor did I really care about the holes she dug herself i</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9203531022062573106">I'm torn as to how to rate this. On the one hand, Fielding nails the humor. Humor is very hard to capture in literature and I often found myself smiling or chuckling. But when I wasn't, I was exasperated with Bridget Jones. Fielding nails her too. Why do women insist on being proud of being so... shallow? Idiotic, blind about themselves and their lives, and obsessed with all the wrong things in life? I didn't sympathize with Bridget at all, nor did I really care about the holes she dug herself into. This book is the perfect example of why I don't read chick lit. I just don't relate to this definition of what women are. More than that, I'm embarrassed by it.<br /><br />I also didn't buy into the love story. I didn't really get why Bridget liked him other than he was there. But what else than a shallow love interest did I expect from Bridget? I'm glad that the Pride and Prejudice undertones were not blatant or I might of cried that Fielding so disgraced the characters. I liked the way Renee Zellweger played Bridget so much more than the way this is written. At least in the movie she has a brain and a personality worth something and she seems a little above all the nonsense around her. One of these days I'd like to read chick lit with a protagonist I can relate to, but then again, would it really be light and chick-lit-ish?</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9203531022062573106">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/3137859?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 02, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/185835-yulia" class="user" title="Yulia">Yulia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/227443.Bridget_Jones_s_Diary" title="Paperback 9780140280098" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/185835-yulia?shelf=here-chicky-chicky" class="actionLinkLite">here-chicky-chicky</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer3137859">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4207071294791017292">This certainly wasn't a novel but, what's worse, it wasn't even a credible diary. Who records their mishaps while cooking and running late in their preparations? Perhaps if this were written in the phone-texting age, I could imagine someone constantly chronicling their every move, no matter how pressing the situation or how inane and empty the commentary, but as it is, this book serves as a frightening precursor to a new generation of books with no established atmosphere, characters, dialogue, o</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4207071294791017292">This certainly wasn't a novel but, what's worse, it wasn't even a credible diary. Who records their mishaps while cooking and running late in their preparations? Perhaps if this were written in the phone-texting age, I could imagine someone constantly chronicling their every move, no matter how pressing the situation or how inane and empty the commentary, but as it is, this book serves as a frightening precursor to a new generation of books with no established atmosphere, characters, dialogue, or insight. Fielding would be better off looking into a crystal ball and telling people their fortunes than writing another non-novel. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4207071294791017292">...more</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/227443.Bridget_Jones_s_Diary" title="Paperback 9780140280098" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4074594-kiki?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4074594-kiki?shelf=sentimental-value" class="actionLinkLite">sentimental-value</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer609019218">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3134397070074364391">Gawd, this book was criminally hilarious. I sat in the doctor's office waiting room literally snorting into my Nine West handbag (there's something really metal about being a minimum wage worker who chooses to buy labels instead of food) as I cradled my Kobo in my lap, with Bridget Jones and her life of ridiculous shenanigans all over the black and white screen. Needless to say, the people I waited with were unimpressed. They are probably not the first to wonder why someone like me would carry a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3134397070074364391">Gawd, this book was criminally hilarious. I sat in the doctor's office waiting room literally snorting into my Nine West handbag (there's something really metal about being a minimum wage worker who chooses to buy labels instead of food) as I cradled my Kobo in my lap, with Bridget Jones and her life of ridiculous shenanigans all over the black and white screen. Needless to say, the people I waited with were unimpressed. They are probably not the first to wonder why someone like me would carry anything as elegant as Nine West.<br /><br />Sometimes I wonder that, too. <br /><br />Honestly? I took off a star because I was highly disappointed with the rushed and nonsensical ending. But the rest of this book? Pure gold. A little warning, though: this is not a shiny, polished tale of the stereotypical (and in real life, extremely rare) uptown and sophisticated south-English thirtysomething. It's an incredibly and often shamefully honest portrayal of a woman who likes sex and cigarettes and drinking and her foul-mouthed friends. It's not <em>The Young Victoria</em>. It's modern Britain, like nobody wants to see it.<br /><br />Sure, it's a little ham-fisted in places. I won't say it doesn't idealize relationships, and get a little bizarre here and there. But who cares? I picked this book up expecting to be entertained. It exceeded those expectations.<br /><br />Good job, Helen Fielding.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <a href="/user/show/23184292-hunger-for-knowledge" class="user" title="Hunger For Knowledge">Hunger For Knowledge</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6342773-bridget-jones-s-diary" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/23184292-hunger-for-knowledge?shelf=chick-lit" class="actionLinkLite">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/23184292-hunger-for-knowledge?shelf=humor" class="actionLinkLite">humor</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/23184292-hunger-for-knowledge?shelf=husbands-credit-card-paid-ebook" class="actionLinkLite">husbands-credit-card-paid-ebook</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/23184292-hunger-for-knowledge?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/23184292-hunger-for-knowledge?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer703560312">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10162228870247428956">Bridget Jones's Diary was a book that had been on my TBR-list for years, it was a goddamn time for me to finally pick it up before the year ends. I've seen the movies but never thought much of them. They are okay, easy fun but very much forgettable. I was hoping the book would make the home run with me but unfortunately not.<br /><br />BJD is a book that Cosmopolitan would most likely describe as a fantastic and cute must-read for every single girl out there. It's not as there would be anything wrong with t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10162228870247428956">Bridget Jones's Diary was a book that had been on my TBR-list for years, it was a goddamn time for me to finally pick it up before the year ends. I've seen the movies but never thought much of them. They are okay, easy fun but very much forgettable. I was hoping the book would make the home run with me but unfortunately not.<br /><br />BJD is a book that Cosmopolitan would most likely describe as a fantastic and cute must-read for every single girl out there. It's not as there would be anything wrong with the magazine, I have read fair amount of its issues, but I most definitely am grown out of its lousy sex and relationship advice sections. In other words, this is a Cosmopolitan book.<br /><br />Bridget herself is quite likable character most of the time, and when not, she is at least a tolerable one. She is witty and in some sense a walking disaster in the most funniest way. <br /><br />But there was too much obsession over weight, and naturally, over men. I actually thought her life outside that was pretty interesting and I would of have enjoyed this more if it would of have been more that than the desperate need to be something else than a single girl living satisfying life without men in sight.<br /><br />The group around Bridget was fantastic. Her friends and family were the most entertaining part of the book, and the reason why I kept going with my reading. <br /><br />There was a lot of insightful observations between singleton and married life. There was times when I laughed and actually enjoyed my time but as a whole this just did not hit the spot I thought it would.<br /><br />The writing was really awful most of the time, but that's intentional as this is a diary, not an grammar exam.<br /><br />I was not planning to finish any more books this year but I just could not start my reading year with a book worth of 2 shiny stars.<br /><br />Also posted at: <a rel="nofollow" href="http://hfk.booklikes.com/" target="_blank">http://hfk.booklikes.com/</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10162228870247428956">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_134110770">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/134110770" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4218875-kwesi" class="left imgcol" title="Kwesi ???"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1402930457p2/4218875.jpg" alt="Kwesi ???" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/134110770?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 16, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4218875-kwesi" class="user" title="Kwesi ???">Kwesi ???</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/227443.Bridget_Jones_s_Diary" title="Paperback 9780140280098" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4218875-kwesi?shelf=owned" class="actionLinkLite">owned</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4218875-kwesi?shelf=helen-fielding" class="actionLinkLite">helen-fielding</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4218875-kwesi?shelf=2012" class="actionLinkLite">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer134110770">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18419870105456212792"><strong>I am not Bridget Jones!</strong><br /><br />My classmate beside me opened a cool notebook with a red leather jacket and a heart sculpted in the middle. I asked her what she's writing in her notebook while my professor keep on talking about carbohydrates, ruminants, and whatever scientific words with -lysis in the end. Because everyone is bored and so do I, I kept on sneaking her notebook and she kept on hiding it. Sorry, playing inside the classroom is illegal but my rules, my rules!<br /><br />So I asked here face-to-face, as</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18419870105456212792"><strong>I am not Bridget Jones!</strong><br /><br />My classmate beside me opened a cool notebook with a red leather jacket and a heart sculpted in the middle. I asked her what she's writing in her notebook while my professor keep on talking about carbohydrates, ruminants, and whatever scientific words with -lysis in the end. Because everyone is bored and so do I, I kept on sneaking her notebook and she kept on hiding it. Sorry, playing inside the classroom is illegal but my rules, my rules!<br /><br />So I asked here face-to-face, as if I'm <em>Boy Abunda</em> and she's <em>Tony Gonzaga</em> talking about <em>Piolo Pascual</em>. <em>
  video&gt;</em> Oops! Okay, back to her. So I asked her if that was her diary and she said yes. Okay, so yeah, it was her diary and my curiosity wanted to jump so high. So when she lean beside her friend, I open her notebook and, <em>Voila!</em>, I can't understand her handwritten. Stupid and I remembered... <em>Bridget Jones's Diary</em>.<br /><br />What's with this book that everyone is reading it, I find it corny, boring and I can't relate a thing, and my friend said because I'm a guy not a girl like Bridget. So I asked her that not all girls are like Bridget and she tweeted me, <em>"My weight (and body) = frustrations in life"</em>. I got her point but she's not that fat and she had an average height of a Filipina. She's cool and a total geek. Maybe she should improve her inner poise to boost her confidence. Does it include confidence? Never mind.<br /><br />So <em>Bridget Jones's Diary</em> is like a normal diary of a frustrated girl who wanted to change and keep her New Year's resolution intact on the first page of her diary. I think everyone doing this but <em>Bridget</em> wanted to change and of course she wanted a boyfriend. This is not a daily dose of everyday writing, somehow... <em>Bridget</em> only write some interesting events in her life. Unlike me, who keep my everyday course in my stupid journal which en up to be a daily to-do list. <em>Ugh!</em> I'm not really good in keeping.<br /><br />Not all books ended happy ending. Well, I don't know with <em>Bridget</em> but I think she got what she wanted in the end except some excess fats she got from too much eating and if all girls can memorize calories of each food like <em>Bridget</em>'s ABC, I find it cool but weird. Do all girl conscious with their sizes and do they really keep track of their boyfriends? Okay. Sorry, I think I just read <em>Bridget</em>'s private notebook. <em>Uhum!</em><br /><br />Next stop... looking for a copy of the movie. Some reviewer and friends said that the movie is better than the book. Here I go again, raiding pirated CDs and illegal videos online. For those like <em>Bridget</em>, there is always a way (and time?) to look (and dispose?) for Mr. Perfect (Mr. Right?). For people like me... I don't have any idea. Just keep believing and do not mind your size. <em>Click! Click!</em> Smile!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="18419870105456212792">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15330141183603117245">I usually end up liking the books better than their film counterparts, but it worked the other way around for Bridget Jones's Diary for me.<br /><br />While I loved the movie, this book was just a bit blah. Bridget irritated me with her whining and her desperation for a man. I hope that I won't be anything like that by the time that I'm nearing the big 3-0. The diary format of the writing annoyed me, but that might just be because I prefer books that are descriptive and have wonderful narrative. <br /><br />Daniel Cleaver also came off as a one-dimensional, total bastard type instead of like the irresistible, though still a bastard, charmer that Hugh Grant portrayed him to be in the movie version. <br /><br />I guess it was an okay short, meaningless read, though. If it had been any longer than it was, I don't think I'd have managed to plod through it.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer13354480">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17673352009179246601">Okay - I learned a few things from this book and I didn't think I would. For me, Ive been doing some pretty heavy reading over the past few weeks -- SWIMMING by Hershon, THE AMBER SPYGLASS bu Pullman. I wanted a break from all that was hard. I wanted to simply read and laugh a little and enjoy a lot. I picked BRIDGET JONES' DIARY because I hoped to read and not engage my intellect too much. Durr...<br /><br />I really, really liked this book, for a number of reasons. Characters that I could relate to -- wei</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17673352009179246601">Okay - I learned a few things from this book and I didn't think I would. For me, Ive been doing some pretty heavy reading over the past few weeks -- SWIMMING by Hershon, THE AMBER SPYGLASS bu Pullman. I wanted a break from all that was hard. I wanted to simply read and laugh a little and enjoy a lot. I picked BRIDGET JONES' DIARY because I hoped to read and not engage my intellect too much. Durr...<br /><br />I really, really liked this book, for a number of reasons. Characters that I could relate to -- weighing oneself every single day. Mooning over a guy and obsessing to the point where you get no work done at work, friends who protect and love you and sometimes lie to you.<br /><br />I thought it probably was a pretty honest assessment of single people in the 1990's. I can't be sure since I haven't been single in over 22 years. <br /><br />This book made me laugh, kept me turning the pages (on my beautiful new SONY E BOOK and kept me interested in Bridget and her group of friends. So, I'm taking anther step and reading the sequel. Very telling because this is not necessarily my favorite genre.<br /><br />Oh yes, it also made me interested in reading other books by English authors. None of the above are bad things.<br /><br /><br />And no - 120-130 pounds is NOT FAT! </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1123829577?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 29, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8406322-desislava" class="user" title="Desislava">Desislava</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/227443.Bridget_Jones_s_Diary" title="Paperback 9780140280098" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8406322-desislava?shelf=chick-lit" class="actionLinkLite">chick-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1123829577">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16947219669017878505">I enjoyed this book, because it showed how an average single woman goes through struggles with empowering herself. <br /><br />I think the main problem I had with this novel is the fact that it's not really a novel. As far as I understand it is based on two years' worth of columns Helen Fielding had written for a British newspaper. The readers of such a serial are bound to expect the same people week after week, and the odds that Bridget will change in response to her experiences are really small. Also I've</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16947219669017878505">I enjoyed this book, because it showed how an average single woman goes through struggles with empowering herself. <br /><br />I think the main problem I had with this novel is the fact that it's not really a novel. As far as I understand it is based on two years' worth of columns Helen Fielding had written for a British newspaper. The readers of such a serial are bound to expect the same people week after week, and the odds that Bridget will change in response to her experiences are really small. Also I've watched the movie before and actually the movie was funnier. I've got to say, there aren't many times when I like the movie better then the book, but this was one.</span>

        rated it

            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/16981538-oana?shelf=british-accent-guys-are-the-best" class="actionLinkLite">british-accent-guys-are-the-best</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer867025325">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1163220408166278955">There isn’t anything I could possibly say about <em>Bridget Jones's Diary</em> which wasn’t already said, so I will keep it simple. <em>Bridget Jones</em> takes the phenomenon known as chick-lit to a completely different level. If you have no idea who Bridget Jones is, nor you know nothing about the premise of the book/movie, that means you’re just an alien-spy, sent on Earth with genocide and forced-colonization purposes, so you don’t even deserve to know. All I can say is (and I guess I’m speaking for the entir</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1163220408166278955">There isn’t anything I could possibly say about <em>Bridget Jones's Diary</em> which wasn’t already said, so I will keep it simple. <em>Bridget Jones</em> takes the phenomenon known as chick-lit to a completely different level. If you have no idea who Bridget Jones is, nor you know nothing about the premise of the book/movie, that means you’re just an alien-spy, sent on Earth with genocide and forced-colonization purposes, so you don’t even deserve to know. All I can say is (and I guess I’m speaking for the entire female specie out there) that there is a moment in every woman’s life when a certain amount of inner Bridget is revealed.<br /><br />I’m a declared everlasting fan of the movie for the obvious reason, meaning the incredible choice of actors, Bridget-Daniel-Mark (hello Mr. Firth, how are you, I’m a big fan), and though the movie is more complex in which the scenario and witty dialogues are concerned, I loved the book too. Quick read, full of Briticisms and British humor I cannot help but love, and the writing style was hilarious to the core. Yes, Mrs. Fielding, I will have some more of Bridget, thank you.<br /></span>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/254774705?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 02, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7310392-sarah" class="user" title="Sarah">Sarah</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/227443.Bridget_Jones_s_Diary" title="Paperback 9780140280098" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer254774705">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11547053383818115422">I read this book a number of years ago after it was recommended to me by a friend and ever since that moment I have been wishing that I could go back in time and smack her over the head and tell her to take the book and shove it.<br /><br />I found the book to be deeply irritating with a central character that was nether funny nor likable. In any way shape or form. In fact Bridget Jones has got to be one of the worst literary characters I have ever come across as she is in turns a moaning, whiny, boring, in</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11547053383818115422">I read this book a number of years ago after it was recommended to me by a friend and ever since that moment I have been wishing that I could go back in time and smack her over the head and tell her to take the book and shove it.<br /><br />I found the book to be deeply irritating with a central character that was nether funny nor likable. In any way shape or form. In fact Bridget Jones has got to be one of the worst literary characters I have ever come across as she is in turns a moaning, whiny, boring, inane, deeply shallow, smug and extremely tedious individual.<br /><br />In the course of reading this book I found myself not caring about her or her irritating 'problems' and at many points I simply rolled my eyes at her stupid behaviour which in turn made me unable to warm to any of the other characters (although I think that was also down to the fact that they don't have an original bone in their fictional bodies) in a story that is essentially nothing more than girl meets boy, girl has difficulty getting boy, has a dalliance with someone else and then eventually get's the boy. With a lot of unnecessary profanity, naval gazing and whinging along the way.<br /><br />It's chick lit of the worst kind and how anyone can hold it up as a book about the difficulties faced by modern (feminist) women is beyond me. If I ever came across a 'Bridget' in real life then I would be deeply concerned for the human race as all the book is concerned about is appearance, getting a man, swearing and sex.<br /><br />Completely devoid of humanity substance and totally misses the point about the troubles of dealing with the difficulties faced by real modern women in everyday life. Best avoided!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11547053383818115422">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer40813687">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18022943835188380228">Judging by some of the reviews, I think its quite possible that it might be slighlty lost on the audience if not a Brit or spent time there. The book was such a success because she nailed the English sensibility, particularly, but not exclusivley female. Everyone either has an element of Bridget in them or knows someone like that. We do whinge, worry about the size of our arses, have to put up with naf jumpers for Christmas, occasionaly about having no friends and found alone eaten by alsations</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18022943835188380228">Judging by some of the reviews, I think its quite possible that it might be slighlty lost on the audience if not a Brit or spent time there. The book was such a success because she nailed the English sensibility, particularly, but not exclusivley female. Everyone either has an element of Bridget in them or knows someone like that. We do whinge, worry about the size of our arses, have to put up with naf jumpers for Christmas, occasionaly about having no friends and found alone eaten by alsations or similar, have obsessions about random people we probably shouldnt and wonder if we will get to shag them, suffer for being a singleton when we secretly rather enjoy it, plan diets that we never quite stick too and sometimes record the banal details. We also often enjoy a good wallow in self-pity. I even have a friend whos more than likely downed several solitary bottles of red and mouthed the words to 'all by myself' before collapsing in stupor. In short theres a bit of Bridge in all of us and I loved it...even if I've now left the country for a slightly less depressing life in the sun!</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1198494254?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 23, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/21992464-helen-the-bookowl" class="user" title="helen the bookowl">helen the bookowl</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1198494254">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1328439638648083326">I think it goes without saying that this is a very funny and witty book, and the main character Bridget Jones is one of the most relatable characters I've read about. I especially liked her intros to every diary entry where we get to know how much she weighs, how many calories she's had during the day, how many cigarettes she has smoken, etc. It was fantastic and actually made me feel quite good about myself, because apparently I'm not the only one with those kind of insecurities. <br />I have watched</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1328439638648083326">I think it goes without saying that this is a very funny and witty book, and the main character Bridget Jones is one of the most relatable characters I've read about. I especially liked her intros to every diary entry where we get to know how much she weighs, how many calories she's had during the day, how many cigarettes she has smoken, etc. It was fantastic and actually made me feel quite good about myself, because apparently I'm not the only one with those kind of insecurities. <br />I have watched the movie adaption of this book several times and I will say that decreaed my reading experience a little bit. I didn't laugh as much at all of the jokes and whimsical twists because I knew they were coming - however, I did laugh out loud once because Bridget's tone of voice and sense of dry humour is amazing. <br />This is a book that will make you feel good - especially if you are of the female species, even though I'm pretty sure males would find it very entertaining and educating as well :-)</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1328439638648083326">...more</a>

      <span id="like_container_review_38382087" class="likeItContainer"><a href="/rating/voters/38382087?resource_type=Review" rel="nofollow" id="like_count_review_38382087"><span class="likesCount">13 likes</span></a> · <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F578596.Bridget_Jones_s_Diary" class="jsLike like_it gr-button gr-button--small" rel="nofollow">Like</a></span> · <a href="/review/show/38382087?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1">see review</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_551014709">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/551014709" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/11240703-k-p-webster" class="left imgcol" title="K.P. Webster"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442877154p2/11240703.jpg" alt="K.P. Webster" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/551014709?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 03, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/11240703-k-p-webster" class="user" title="K.P. Webster">K.P. Webster</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/227443.Bridget_Jones_s_Diary" title="Paperback 9780140280098" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/11240703-k-p-webster?shelf=books-i-have-considered-burning" class="actionLinkLite">books-i-have-considered-burning</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer551014709">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14760516150969523242">What a depressingly bad book. ‘Helen Fielding is one of the funniest writers in Britain,’ says Nick Hornby on the front cover, ‘and Bridget Jones is a creation of comic genius.’ What in earth…? Why is he saying that? Did he want to sleep with her? Same goes for Salman Rushdie. ‘A brilliant comic creation,' blurbs Salman. 'Even men will laugh.’ Oh, Salman. Why is he saying that? Surely, if a book is genuinely funny, then people will laugh irrespective of their gender. Obviously. ‘Even men will la</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14760516150969523242">What a depressingly bad book. ‘Helen Fielding is one of the funniest writers in Britain,’ says Nick Hornby on the front cover, ‘and Bridget Jones is a creation of comic genius.’ What in earth…? Why is he saying that? Did he want to sleep with her? Same goes for Salman Rushdie. ‘A brilliant comic creation,' blurbs Salman. 'Even men will laugh.’ Oh, Salman. Why is he saying that? Surely, if a book is genuinely funny, then people will laugh irrespective of their gender. Obviously. ‘Even men will laugh.’ What kind of bullshit is that? As it happens, I did laugh. I laughed, if I remember correctly, four times. Out loud. On the other hand, I also shouted out in anger, annoyance and plain old despair at least forty times.<br /><br />So what’s wrong with this book?<br /><br />Well, in a nutshell: flaccid, half-dimensional characterisation; sickeningly pat plotting – the ending in particular is an embarrassing slap in the face for anyone who's ever shown even a passing consideration for the real world; downright adolescent ideas about style – those bits where she writes ‘drunk’ and ends up with her typing slurred are a disgrace. <br /><br />Also, I know Helen Fielding can’t exactly be blamed for this, but Jesus, you’d think Picador could afford a decent proof reader. There are so many incredible howlers in BJD that it beggars belief. On page 174 of this edition, for example… <br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380411887r/809673._SX540_SY540_.jpg" /><br /><br />…not only is there an ‘on one’ instead of a ‘no one’, but there is also – drum roll – this: ‘that’s a nice shirt <em>your</em> wearing’. NOOOOOoooooooo! God in Heaven, strike me down and bugger me.<br /><br />One thing that particularly upset me about this book - and which Helen Fielding can be blamed for - was the woefully predictable oscillation of mood. This kind of thing throughout: <br /><br /><blockquote>7pm. Opened bottle of wine feeling desperate and lonely and miserable. 7.30pm. Oh unassailable joy! Daniel called and declared his undying love for me. 8pm. Daniel called back and said he’d called the wrong number by mistake. He thought I was Ryan Giggs. (Who?) Opened second bottle of wine. Binged on marshmallow and lard and put on 3 stone in 20 minutes. 9pm. Oh insurmountable ecstasy! Mark Darcy called and declared his undying love for me. He’s coming over. Performed quick gastric bypass procedure on self and washed hair. Down to 9 stone but still look podgy. 10.30pm. Mark Darcy stood me up. Why am I so lonely? Why? Why? Why? </blockquote><br /><br />Because you’re a bore, Bridget, that’s why. You’re a fucking bore.<br /><br />Of course I know we don’t have to like our fictional protagonists. Patrick Bateman, for example, is vile. As is Humbert Humbert, and even Homer Simpson. Yet in each of these cases, it is possible to describe these characters using one or more of the following adjectives: ‘interesting’, ‘fascinating’, ‘funny’ or ‘well-written’. And all of these things are important. However, if you insist on creating a character who is dull, slow-witted, utterly charmless, and self-indulgent to the point of mentally ill, then you’d better make sure that you write them well. Otherwise no one will read your book.<br /><br />So, I suppose the next question has to be: how could I believe so passionately that what I’m saying is true and yet at the same time be so wildly and obviously wrong?<br /><br /><em>Bridget Jones's Diary</em> has apparently sold millions and millions and millions of copies worldwide. It has also picked up astonishing reviews by the likes of the inestimable Jilly Cooper and a clearly fuckstruck Salman Rushdie.<br /><br />My instinct is to say that these people are all wrong and that I know dross when I read it and that <em>Bridget Jones’s Diary</em> is utter, utter dross. But… what if it’s me?<br /><br />This is a chilling thought. And I'm not sure what to do with it. Perhaps I shall just sit here, in my study, in nothing but the light from my computer monitor, and weep.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14760516150969523242">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_24717570">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/24717570" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/472694-e" class="left imgcol" title="E"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1201447841p2/472694.jpg" alt="E" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/24717570?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 25, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/472694-e" class="user" title="E">E</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/856684.Bridget_Jones_s_Diary" title="Paperback 9780330371636" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/472694-e?shelf=novels" class="actionLinkLite">novels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer24717570'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer24717570">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13821180449642379745">For me, reading this book was exactly like watching a season of "Ally McBeal" - when I laughed, I laughed outloud and thoroughly enjoyed myself. And occasionally I did allow myself to care who ends up with whom. But I held a grudge against the main character throughout for being so ludicrously insecure and vulnerable to vulgar materialism. <br /><br />Like Ally, Bridget is a self-proclaimed feminist who cannot hold onto a single tenet of the concept long enough to spare herself any plummets on her emotional</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13821180449642379745">For me, reading this book was exactly like watching a season of "Ally McBeal" - when I laughed, I laughed outloud and thoroughly enjoyed myself. And occasionally I did allow myself to care who ends up with whom. But I held a grudge against the main character throughout for being so ludicrously insecure and vulnerable to vulgar materialism. <br /><br />Like Ally, Bridget is a self-proclaimed feminist who cannot hold onto a single tenet of the concept long enough to spare herself any plummets on her emotional rollercoaster of second-guessing and self-scrutiny. Many of the women with which she surrounds herself are in fact far more self-confident than she is, but there are no signs of it rubbing off. <br /><br />Of course I was satisfied that in the end she was swept away by a diamond in the rough instead of the first greasy charmer, but it annoyed me to no end that she was so very passively swept away. Although Mark Darcy did let her know how impressed he was with her profile as a well-read feminist and her willingness to show up at a party in a bunny suit, she prefers to tell her diary what a turn-on it is to see him take control of her mother's legal fate in a swaggering, authoritarian way. Like Ally McBeal, Bridget does not see a boyfriend as a partner but rather the constant cat to her mouse.<br /><br />It's hard to be a working, single woman in today's modern society - yes. It's difficult to find a soul mate amid all the social pressure to simply find someone - yes. But obsessing over weight, appearance, and everyone else's opinion of you is an adolescent phase that can and must be overcome. Otherwise, on the microcosmic level, feminism has failed you and it's dishonest to claim it as a guise.<br /><br />Despite that however, dishonesty can still make for a very funny, light read. I picked this book because the theme of infanticide in the other novel I had going was getting to be too much for me, and on that level it did not disappoint.<br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13821180449642379745">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1717131603939497184">if any of the characters from this book had been born two centuries earlier, they'd have died any number of Oregon Trail-like deaths or perhaps been sensibly culled in armed conflict. they'd have had a right to bitch up this bitchstorm like three bitches in a bitchboat, but unable to find publication, because Victorian England had the good breeding and stiff upper lip to send squealing little piglets like Bridget Jones into the convent, and her tribe of gormless chav fratboys would have been too</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1717131603939497184">if any of the characters from this book had been born two centuries earlier, they'd have died any number of Oregon Trail-like deaths or perhaps been sensibly culled in armed conflict. they'd have had a right to bitch up this bitchstorm like three bitches in a bitchboat, but unable to find publication, because Victorian England had the good breeding and stiff upper lip to send squealing little piglets like Bridget Jones into the convent, and her tribe of gormless chav fratboys would have been too busy dodging impressment gangs and learning euclidean geometry to engage in all this raffishness.<br /><br />I only award it a third star because I one time was at this horrible party, and the following conversation ensued:<br /><br /><strong>intolerable guy:</strong> I feel silly but I'm reading <em>Bridget Jones's Diary</em>; <strong>unoffensive SO of iTG</strong> just read it---<br /><strong>uSO-iTG</strong>: I loved the movie and then I thought the book was great---<br /><strong>iTG</strong>: so I borrowed it when she was done---<br /><strong>nick black</strong>: y'all went and saw a movie version of <em>Bridget Jones's Diary</em>?!?! jesus?! do you support the doctrine of racial holy war?<br /><strong>all</strong>: ???<br /><strong>nick black</strong>: you know, 14 words, etc...i mean, i'm not the one reading <em>Bridget Jones's Diary</em>...<br /><strong>all</strong>: ???<br /><strong>nick black</strong>: oh! my goodness! excuse me i thought you meant <a title="These Is My Words by Nancy E. Turner" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/348225.These_Is_My_Words">The Turner Diaries</a>, William Luther Pierce's controversial white power thriller. hah! i don't know what i could have been thinking.<br /><strong>iTG</strong>: no.<br /><strong>nick black</strong>: right right, Bridget Jones is about fornication, not extremism!<br /><br />so yeah, that conversation was pretty much derailed.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_616834458">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/616834458" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/16458477-tina" class="left imgcol" title="Tina"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1446553627p2/16458477.jpg" alt="Tina" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/616834458?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 12, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/16458477-tina" class="user" title="Tina">Tina</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/533744.Bridget_Jones_s_Diary" title="Hardcover 9780670880720" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/16458477-tina?shelf=owned-books" class="actionLinkLite">owned-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer616834458">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2636363348373165630">I've had this book on my shelf for a while now, when all of a sudden I feel an urge to drop the books I'm currently reading and just go with <em>Bridget Jones's Diary</em>. Having watched the movie about a gazillion times prior to reading the book (yes, a guilty pleasure I'm not ashamed of), I was quite prepared what to expect, and was a bit skeptical as to whether I'll like it that much now that I'm spoiled. But girl, did I like that book! Although in a format of a very untypical diary, the book gives a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2636363348373165630">I've had this book on my shelf for a while now, when all of a sudden I feel an urge to drop the books I'm currently reading and just go with <em>Bridget Jones's Diary</em>. Having watched the movie about a gazillion times prior to reading the book (yes, a guilty pleasure I'm not ashamed of), I was quite prepared what to expect, and was a bit skeptical as to whether I'll like it that much now that I'm spoiled. But girl, did I like that book! Although in a format of a very untypical diary, the book gives a very, <u>very</u> realistic idea of how women feel about themselves, their relationships with friends/family/men and their lives in general. Not sure if this matches what I categorize as chick-lit in my head, but who cares anyway? I really, really liked that book and definitely recommend it. It's a very quick read, it's totally relatable and very funny. Gotta go now, the movie is waiting.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2636363348373165630">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1369774446">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1369774446" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/31502192-francesca" class="left imgcol" title="Francesca"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1446156110p2/31502192.jpg" alt="Francesca" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1369774446?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 04, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/31502192-francesca" class="user" title="Francesca">Francesca</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/25985553-bridget-jones-s-diary" title="Paperback 9781447288930" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/31502192-francesca?shelf=2015-reading-challenge" class="actionLinkLite">2015-reading-challenge</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/31502192-francesca?shelf=humour" class="actionLinkLite">humour</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/31502192-francesca?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/31502192-francesca?shelf=characters-i-can-t-stand" class="actionLinkLite">characters-i-can-t-stand</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/31502192-francesca?shelf=female-authors" class="actionLinkLite">female-authors</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/31502192-francesca?shelf=200-to-400-pages" class="actionLinkLite">200-to-400-pages</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/31502192-francesca?shelf=made-into-a-movie-or-tv-show" class="actionLinkLite">made-into-a-movie-or-tv-show</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/31502192-francesca?shelf=drama" class="actionLinkLite">drama</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1369774446">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17485396036618618356">I put off writing this review because I knew it was just going to end up being an angry rant and I didn't want to offend anyone that loved this book, but the time has come. I now warn those who loved the book to, please, either look away now or read ahead with caution. No offense is meant at all to people who enjoyed this book.<br /><br />I will start by saying that I had seen the movie before reading the book. I've seen the movie quite a few times (the second one only once or twice). It's the kind of movie</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17485396036618618356">I put off writing this review because I knew it was just going to end up being an angry rant and I didn't want to offend anyone that loved this book, but the time has come. I now warn those who loved the book to, please, either look away now or read ahead with caution. No offense is meant at all to people who enjoyed this book.<br /><br />I will start by saying that I had seen the movie before reading the book. I've seen the movie quite a few times (the second one only once or twice). It's the kind of movie that I enjoy enough that if I happen to spot it on TV, I will sit and watch it quite happily. It's never been a movie that I've gone out of my way to watch or one that I would sit there and suddenly think 'I know, I'll stick that on' but I do enjoy it when I watch it as a nice, cutesy, light movie. So I decided to give the book a try and see if I'd enjoy it even more. Well, that didn't happen. Every single character is more likable in the movie than in the book. Every single one of them. I've never been that fond of Renee Zellweger in the role but even she was more likable than book Bridget, and the effortless combined charm of Hugh Grant and Colin Firth make both male suitors much more attractive and make it easier for us to understand why Bridget would actually go for either of them because just in writing, both men are incredibly unappealing.<br /><br />Mark Darcy has his good moments and I will admit to their being a few moments where I thought 'aaww he's quite sweet' but it never went beyond that and for most of the book (basically the whole book) he was such a wet fish and unfortunately an incredibly dull character. He didn't do anything. He stood up for Bridget, maybe, twice in the whole book and besides that he just stood by silently and did what everyone else told him he should do. He was barely even in the book for the most part which just made him getting together with Bridget seem so random and rushed at the end.<br /><br />Daniel Cleaver is just the worst. I mean, I know he's supposed to be because he's supposed to be the worst human being ever so that we root for boring old Mark Darcy but still. It was almost over the top with just how horrible he was the whole time. I understand that, yes, sometimes women do unfortunately fall for horrible guys and can't help it but while I was reading it I just could not for the life of me ever work out why Bridget liked him so much and let him treat her like such crap.<br /><br />Onto Bridget herself, oh god. Where do I even start? Actually let's start with the whole weight thing because this really pissed me off. First of all, there were several times when she would be about 9 stone and would complain about being 'basically obese'. Erm, I'm sorry, what?! 9 stone is not obese, it's not even close. If a girl who is overweight (and weighs more than 9 stone) reads this book and sees Bridget moaning about being 9 stone and complaining about how 'gross' and 'fat' she is, how would that then make them feel? But it doesn't stop there because when Bridget finally does loose some weight and drop a stone, her friends (who are all horrible) tell her she looks tired and unhealthy. Secondly, I don't mind someone complaining about not being able to lose weight when it's obvious that they're making a genuine effort to but when someone moans about being "overweight" and says they want to lose weight but then immediately eats loads of chocolate or goes out binge drinking it is the most frustrating thing to read or listen to ever. Why should I feel any sympathy for someone who just complains all the time but doesn't actually do anything to help themselves? She also complains about wanting to cut down on her drinking and give up smoking, and does she do either of those? No, of course she doesn't, she just continues moaning about it.<br /><br />Bridget and her friends are also one of the worst group of friends ever. One of their friends is with some guy that they all hate, and for good reason because he's horrible to their friend and treats her poorly, so what do they do? Nothing. According to Bridget herself, after one of the first break ups their friend had with the guy, Sharon and Bridget told her how much they hated him and that she shouldn't be with him and then the friend got back together with him and told him everything they said. First of all, this shows how horrible all her friends are, even the one being screwed over by the guy then screws her friends over to him, and secondly Bridget and Sharon now use that as their excuse to just blatantly lie to their friends face and support her decision to get back with him whenever she gets dumped by him. These are not true friends. This is far from the only example. Every one of Bridget's friends are horrible, selfish, and self-centred people. The only character I somewhat enjoyed was Sharon and that was just because she kept talking about feminism and standing up for single women (which Bridget would occasionally do in the parts of the book that I actually enjoyed but for he most part she'd just continue moping about the fact that she was still single).<br /><br />Then we get onto the topic of Bridget and her parents. Well, from the start it's clearly evident that Bridget has a favourite and her favourite is her Dad because her Mum is basically the typical cartoon, cheesy sit-com, bitch of a mother who always puts her daughter down or forces her to do things she doesn't want to do like talk to people. This favouritism is fine to start with because you have already been shown Bridget's point of view and you kind of understand it because the Dad is shown as the sweet, caring type of Dad. The favouritism becomes more annoying however when Bridget's Mum decides to leave her Dad. The Mum gives her reasons which are actually very sound, solid, good reasons for having had enough and wanting a divorce (the Dad retired years ago and now does absolutely nothing but he expects her to continue her role as happy housewife and do everything for him and she wants to go out and get a job of her own as she's never had one) but suddenly, feminist and pro-singleton, Bridget doesn't accept those reasons and still sides with the Dad who completely fails to see how he could be in any way at fault for how the Mum feels.<br /><br />[Edit] I initially gave this two stars, as I guess I was feeling generous (I had just come back from holiday, maybe that influenced it) but after leaving it for a while and then thinking about it again, I'm going to have to stick to my guns and give it one star. I did not enjoy this book at all. I spent most of it just feeling so angry at everyone and everything in it. It had some stupid plotlines thrown in out of nowhere (yes, I'm looking at the Mum and her money laundering boyfriend) which just frustrated me more. Some of the book was (I guess sadly in some cases) very realistic. As much as I hated the characters, they did all feel very real and I know that I have definitely known people like some of them in my life. Some parts of the book were also very relatable, as a singleton that has been single for a long time I can definitely say that I've had a lot of the same comments and conversations that Bridget has in the book with various people. How realistic and, sometimes, relatable the book can be/is, is what made me initially give it 2 stars instead of 1 but even with those moments, I still had a bad time reading this book. The main parts I did somewhat enjoy were whenever Bridget was actually having one of her moments of not caring and enjoying being single and throwing it back in people's faces when they tried to talk down to her for it, as that is the way I wish more single women were portrayed in the media as opposed to the sad, desperate women who can't cope or function without a man that they are usually shown to be (i.e. like Bridget through most of the book). So this book wasn't completely without redeeming moments but for the most part I just found this book incredibly hard to swallow. I was looking for a nice, relaxing, funny, holiday read and I didn't get any of those from this book. Obviously other people do enjoy this book and it's sequels so it was clearly just the wrong book for me. The hotel I was staying at had a double sided bookshelf where people could take or leave a book so I left this one there, hopefully it will find it's way into the hands of someone who will enjoy it a lot more than I did.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17485396036618618356">...more</a>
