<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_455679676">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/455679676" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/13266158-samadrita" class="left imgcol" title="Samadrita"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1439470626p2/13266158.jpg" alt="Samadrita" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/455679676?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 14, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/13266158-samadrita" class="user" title="Samadrita">Samadrita</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/227443.Bridget_Jones_s_Diary" title="Paperback 9780140280098" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/13266158-samadrita?shelf=semi-favorites" class="actionLinkLite">semi-favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/13266158-samadrita?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/13266158-samadrita?shelf=for-teh-ladies" class="actionLinkLite">for-teh-ladies</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/13266158-samadrita?shelf=feminism-feminist-undertones" class="actionLinkLite">feminism-feminist-undertones</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/13266158-samadrita?shelf=deliciously-mushy" class="actionLinkLite">deliciously-mushy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/13266158-samadrita?shelf=bring-on-the-lols" class="actionLinkLite">bring-on-the-lols</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer455679676">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12607573545293348256">I have never been a big fan of Bridget Jones to be honest. Renee Zellweger's portrayal of the klutzy, down-on-luck, slightly overweight British singleton in her 30s and her discernibly fake British accent did not help. Sure she received an Academy award nomination for her role, however that does not change my opinion. I only remember the movie for Colin Firth.<br />But this book made me see Bridget in a different light. Sure she is a bit on the pudgy side, clumsy, alcoholic with fabulously bad culinar</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12607573545293348256">I have never been a big fan of Bridget Jones to be honest. Renee Zellweger's portrayal of the klutzy, down-on-luck, slightly overweight British singleton in her 30s and her discernibly fake British accent did not help. Sure she received an Academy award nomination for her role, however that does not change my opinion. I only remember the movie for Colin Firth.<br />But this book made me see Bridget in a different light. Sure she is a bit on the pudgy side, clumsy, alcoholic with fabulously bad culinary skills but she does not discard her self-esteem right away in return for Daniel Cleaver's affections in the beginning. I'm impressed that the author deliberately did not make Bridget the quintessential, <em>'beautifully anorexic'</em> girl but a woman with numerous flaws and yet chose to give her an acute sense of self-importance. Bridget does obsess about losing weight but at least she never goes ballistic trying to lose it or go <em>"I'm so fat"</em> every two seconds. She is more or less happy and comfortable in her skin and that is what separates her from the hordes of chick-lit heroines out there.<br /><br />Bridget's hilarious observations on the problems faced by single women, relationships, married people, her parents' marital woes and even trifles like Christmas presents make this book an absolute laugh riot. Whereas the movie focuses too much on Bridget as a laughably clumsy woman who never gets anything right and I was forced to wonder what Daniel Cleaver and especially Mark Darcy found attractive about her. The book served as the clarification in this case since Mark Darcy clearly states how Bridget is not <em>'lacquered over'</em> like other women which is why he likes her. Whereas in the movie he declares <em>'I like you very much...just as you are'</em> which sounded extremely cliched and unreal in my opinion.<br /><br />I was about 60% through with the novel when the plot started to drag. Bridget and Daniel's relationship went in limbo and I kept waiting for something to happen which would carry the story forward. Then came the bad part when Bridget began screwing up one thing after the other in exceptionally embarrassing ways and I was almost feeling sorry for Mark Darcy for having been designated to end up with her. And the worst part was, how one phone call from Daniel swayed Bridget to the point of momentarily making her forget his shameless infidelity. Hated her for it. That is why the 5-star rating drops to a 4-star in my case.<br />But even so, Bridget Jones is one of the best specimens of chick-lit out there since it is free from the banality of American chick-lit tropes, interlaced with a generous dosage of trademark English humour. And behind the facade of a rom-com, it is able to bring to light a few rather grim aspects of lives of women in their 30s and women in general.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12607573545293348256">...more</a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/13956884?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 29, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/841687-vish" class="user" title="Vish">Vish</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/227443.Bridget_Jones_s_Diary" title="Paperback 9780140280098" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer13956884">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17356210646513458522">I read this book for a contemporary section of an AP Literature Class. <br /><br />To say the least, Fielding sells her soul to the idle masses to sell novels. I believe the only way BJD will be remembered in the literary canon is if the critics of the future look back at what a horrid generation we were. <br /><br />A daughter of the greatest generation, Bridget Jones is an insecure, irresponsible, sex-driven woman who (to be fair) write clever, quippy journal entries of her life. The humor, at best, is a compensation</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17356210646513458522">I read this book for a contemporary section of an AP Literature Class. <br /><br />To say the least, Fielding sells her soul to the idle masses to sell novels. I believe the only way BJD will be remembered in the literary canon is if the critics of the future look back at what a horrid generation we were. <br /><br />A daughter of the greatest generation, Bridget Jones is an insecure, irresponsible, sex-driven woman who (to be fair) write clever, quippy journal entries of her life. The humor, at best, is a compensation to keep the reader from falling asleep from the over-tedious style of the book itself. <br /><br />Based loosley off of Jane Austen's "Pride and Prejudice" (a book which, in my opinion, was 562 pages of enjoyable small talk), this book uses the empathetic "THIS CHARACTER IS ME" plea to force a generation of immorailty and insecurity to flock around it. <br /><br />Still, I think a read can still be enjoyable, even if it isn't necessarily enaging literature. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17356210646513458522">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/3284904-jasmin" class="left imgcol" title="Jasmin"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1351874823p2/3284904.jpg" alt="Jasmin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/93849648?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 06, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3284904-jasmin" class="user" title="Jasmin">Jasmin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/227443.Bridget_Jones_s_Diary" title="Paperback 9780140280098" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People with high tolerance for crap</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3284904-jasmin?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3284904-jasmin?shelf=chick-lit" class="actionLinkLite">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3284904-jasmin?shelf=contemporary-romance" class="actionLinkLite">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3284904-jasmin?shelf=humor" class="actionLinkLite">humor</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3284904-jasmin?shelf=reviewed-by-me" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed-by-me</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3284904-jasmin?shelf=two-stars" class="actionLinkLite">two-stars</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3284904-jasmin?shelf=bbc-top-100" class="actionLinkLite">bbc-top-100</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer93849648">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13000920586234987337">Bridget Jones's Diary was bloody horrible.<br /><br />I once thought of myself as quite an intellectual being, but after reading this book, I felt that it has sucked all the IQ i once had (i refuse to believe that I had none to begin with, haha), since this book felt like a hundred pages of BLAH BLAH going on.<br /><br />I wanted a light read, after literally being in the middle of gun point. I, who has zero tolerance for violence, needed something to cheer myself up. However, this book sucked the humor out of me. I do</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13000920586234987337">Bridget Jones's Diary was bloody horrible.<br /><br />I once thought of myself as quite an intellectual being, but after reading this book, I felt that it has sucked all the IQ i once had (i refuse to believe that I had none to begin with, haha), since this book felt like a hundred pages of BLAH BLAH going on.<br /><br />I wanted a light read, after literally being in the middle of gun point. I, who has zero tolerance for violence, needed something to cheer myself up. However, this book sucked the humor out of me. I don't even remembering laughing even once. I wanted to give the book the benefit of the doubt. Maybe I was just overly traumatized after the gun thing, so I tried reading another book, and bloody hell, I was laughing. So I have to put all the blame on this bloody excuse of a book.<br /><br />I will continue to rant. Ranting is good. I felt no pity for Bridget. I found her absolutely unlikable and highly repulsive. I felt no remorse for her inability to find a boyfriend or manage to fulfill a thing or two on her new year's resolution list.<br /><br />This is the most shallow book I've read, and even I don't see the point of reading it. If it's barely for entertainment, I'm sorry, this book failed. I could only be glad that I finished this sad excuse of a book, though I do regret the time and effort wasted in finishing it. The only reason I gave it two stars, is because I love Mr. Darcy and the hero of this book is named Mark Darcy (though Mark Darcy is in no way comparable to Mr. Darcy in anyway, except by name). And hey, with the two stars, I was being way too generous.<br /><br />Hmm, despite this book not making me laugh, it did help me unleash a little bit of anger and sorrow I feel for having to endure a moment of having a stranger point a gun at my face. But at this point, the gun could have been more desirable than having to endure reading this book once more.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13000920586234987337">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/2908629-ellie" class="left imgcol" title="Ellie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1399799985p2/2908629.jpg" alt="Ellie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1164671248?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 14, 2015</a>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1164671248">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13958611163975588380">Somehow, I've missed reading <a title="Bridget Jones's Diary (Bridget Jones, #1) by Helen Fielding" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/227443.Bridget_Jones_s_Diary__Bridget_Jones___1_">Bridget Jones's Diary</a> by <a title="Helen Fielding" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3090.Helen_Fielding">Helen Fielding</a>. At first, I think I thought it sounded silly. Later, I just forgot about it. So when I saw it on a Kindle sale, I thought, Why not? <br /><br />And I'm so glad I did. It's an hilarious book. I was married with children by the time the book came out but only a few short years before was I somewhat of an American dead-ringer for Bridget. At least, close enough for me to cringe at points (while laughing).<br /><br />I'm not a great reader of comic novel</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13958611163975588380">Somehow, I've missed reading <a title="Bridget Jones's Diary (Bridget Jones, #1) by Helen Fielding" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/227443.Bridget_Jones_s_Diary__Bridget_Jones___1_">Bridget Jones's Diary</a> by <a title="Helen Fielding" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3090.Helen_Fielding">Helen Fielding</a>. At first, I think I thought it sounded silly. Later, I just forgot about it. So when I saw it on a Kindle sale, I thought, Why not? <br /><br />And I'm so glad I did. It's an hilarious book. I was married with children by the time the book came out but only a few short years before was I somewhat of an American dead-ringer for Bridget. At least, close enough for me to cringe at points (while laughing).<br /><br />I'm not a great reader of comic novels-few novels make me laugh. And, while Bridget Jones didn't have me guffawing out loud, it often made me smile. <br /><br />Somehow, I'd missed the comparison with Jane Austen, despite Darcy's name being, well, Darcy. Bridget is more an Emma than an Elizabeth but she's smart and funny. I think that the book stands better on its own, since comparisons with Austen are hard to live up to and the book does just fine. Not maybe one for the ages but a delight even twenty years after its time.<br /><br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }

    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked

    }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {

  }

In an age when every standard of decent cond&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText3496880858842532574\" style=\"display:none\"&gt;It is customary, I have noticed, in publishing an autobiography to preface it with some sort of apology. But there are times, and surely the present is one of them, when to do so is manifestly unnecessary. In an age when every standard of decent conduct has either been torn down or is threatened with destruction; when every newspaper is daily reporting scenes of violence, divorce, and arson; when quite young girls smoke cigarettes and even, I am assured, sometimes cigars; when mature women, the mothers of unhappy children, enter the sea in one-piece bathing-costumes; and when married men, the heads of households, prefer the flicker of the cinematograph to the Athanasian Creed -- then it is obviously a task, not to be justifiably avoided, to place some higher example before the world. For some time -- I am now forty-seven -- I had been feeling this with increasing urgency. And when not only my wife and her four sisters, but the vicar of my parish, the Reverend Simeon Whey, approached me with the same suggestion, I felt that delay would amount to sin. That sin, by many persons, is now lightly regarded, I am, of course, only too well aware. That its very existence is denied by others is a fact equally familiar to me. But I am not one of them. On every ground I am an unflinching opponent of sin. I have continually rebuked it in others. I have strictly refrained from it in myself. And for that reason alone I have deemed it incumbent upon me to issue this volume. A satire, originally anonymous, first published in the United Kingdom in May 1924 and, later that year in the United States.     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3090.Helen_Fielding">About Helen Fielding</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/3090.Helen_Fielding"><img alt="3090" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1381158323p2/3090.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer4571304823791471077">Helen Fielding was born in Yorkshire. She worked for many years in London as a newspaper and TV journalist, travelling as wildly and as often as possibly to Africa, India and Central America. She is the author of four novels: Cause Celeb, Bridget Jones’ s Diary, Bridget Jones:The Edge of Reason and Olivia Joules and the Overactive Imagination, and co-wrote the screenplays for the movie of Bridget</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4571304823791471077">Helen Fielding was born in Yorkshire. She worked for many years in London as a newspaper and TV journalist, travelling as wildly and as often as possibly to Africa, India and Central America. She is the author of four novels: Cause Celeb, Bridget Jones’ s Diary, Bridget Jones:The Edge of Reason and Olivia Joules and the Overactive Imagination, and co-wrote the screenplays for the movie of Bridget Jones’s Diary and the sequel based on The Edge of Reason. She now works full-time as a novelist and screenwriter and lives in London and Los Angeles. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4571304823791471077">...more</a>

    </div>
